The game is known in several countries under different names.\r\nPlayers alternate turns placing a stone of their color on an empty intersection. The winner is the first player to form an unbroken chain of five stones horizontally, vertically, or diagonally.\r\nIt originated in Japan during the Heian period[citation needed]. The name \"Gomoku\" is from the Japanese language, in which it is referred to as gomokunarabe (‰∫îÁõÆ‰∏¶„Åπ). Go means five, moku is a counter word for pieces and narabe means line-up. The game is also popular in Korea, where it is called omok (Ïò§Î™© [‰∫îÁõÆ]) which has the same structure and origin as the Japanese name.\r\nThe Japanese call this game Go-moku (five stones). In the nineteenth century, the game was introduced to Britain where it was known as Go Bang, said to be a corruption of the Japanese word goban, said to be adopted from Chinese k'i pan (q√≠ p√°n)
